use \u003ca href=\"https://www.twilio.com/sms\"\u003eProgrammable SMS\u003c/a\u003e to send SMS and MMS messages in your Java web application. The code snippets in this guide are written using the Java SDK 7 or higher, and make use of the \u003ca href=\"/docs/libraries/java\"\u003eTwilio Java SDK\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eLet's get started!\u003c/p\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"block-rich_text \"\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"rich-text\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"block-rich_text \"\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"rich-text\"\u003e\u003ch2 id=\"sign-up-for-a-twilio-account\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"toclink\" href=\"#sign-up-for-a-twilio-account\"\u003eSign up for a Twilio Account\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003eTo use the Twilio \u003ca href=\"/docs/api/rest\"\u003eREST API\u003c/a\u003e, you need an account. \u003ca href=\"/try-twilio\"\u003eSigning up for a free Twilio account\u003c/a\u003e is easy. Once you've signed up, head over to your \u003ca href=\"/console\"\u003eConsole\u003c/a\u003e and grab your Account SID and your Auth Token. You will need those for the code samples below.\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2 id=\"purchase-an-sms-capable-phone-number\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"toclink\" href=\"#purchase-an-sms-capable-phone-number\"\u003ePurchase an SMS Capable Phone Number\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003eSending SMS messages requires an SMS capable phone number. You can \u003ca href=\"https://www.twilio.com/console/phone-numbers/search\"\u003ebrowse the available phone numbers\u003c/a\u003e in the Console. Be sure that the phone number you buy is SMS capable. When you search, you can check the box to filter available numbers to those that are SMS capable:\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eWhen viewing the search results, you can see the capability icons in the list of available numbers:\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eArmed with a Twilio phone number, you can now start sending messages to mobile devices.\u003c/p\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"block-rich_text \"\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"rich-text\"\u003e\u003ch2 id=\"send-an-sms-message-via-the-rest-api\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"toclink\" href=\"#send-an-sms-message-via-the-rest-api\"\u003eSend an SMS Message via the REST API\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003eSending an outgoing SMS message requires sending an HTTP POST to the \u003ca href=\"/docs/api/rest/message\"\u003eMessages resource URI\u003c/a\u003e. Using the helper library, you can create a new instance of the \u003cb\u003eMessage\u003c/b\u003e resource and specify the \u003cb\u003eTo\u003c/b\u003e, \u003cb\u003eFrom\u003c/b\u003e, and \u003cb\u003eBody\u003c/b\u003e parameters for your message.\u003c/p\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"block-code_sample \"\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"md-code-sample\" class=\"button-mode\"\u003e\n\u003ch5 class=\"title\"\u003e\n\u003ci class=\"fa fa-fw fa-code\"\u003e\u003c/i\u003e\n      Send an SMS using the Programmable SMS API\n    \u003c/h5\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"active-tail\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"block-rich_text \"\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"rich-text\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eIf you want to send a message to several recipients, you could simply create an array of recipients and iterate through each phone number in that array. You can send as many messages as you like, as fast as you like and Twilio will queue them up for delivery at your \u003ca href=\"/help/faq/twilio-basics/how-many-calls-and-sms-messages-per-second-can-my-twilio-account-make?baseUrl=%2Fhelp%2F\"\u003eprescribed rate limit\u003c/a\u003e. See our guide on how to \u003ca href=\"/docs/guides/sms/how-to-send-bulk-sms-messages-in-java\"\u003eSend Bulk SMS Messages\u003c/a\u003e for more tips.\u003c/p\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"block-rich_text \"\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"rich-text\"\u003e\u003ch2 id=\"send-a-message-with-media-mms\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"toclink\" href=\"#send-a-message-with-media-mms\"\u003eSend a Message with Media (MMS)\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003eIt's also easy to send an outgoing MMS using Twilio. To send an MMS, you also make an HTTP POST request to the \u003ca href=\"/docs/api/rest/message\"\u003eMessages resource\u003c/a\u003e but this time specify a parameter for the URL of media, such as an image.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003ci\u003eMMS messages can only be sent and received by numbers having MMS capability.\u003c/i\u003e You can \u003ca href=\"/console/phone-numbers/search\"\u003echeck the capabilities\u003c/a\u003e of numbers in the account portal or query the \u003ca href=\"/docs/api/rest/available-phone-numbers\"\u003eAvailable Phone Numbers\u003c/a\u003e resource to search for Twilio numbers that are MMS enabled.\u003c/p\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"block-code_sample \"\u003e\n\u003cdiv \u003cdiv\u003e\u003cdiv\u003e\u003cp\u003eIn this guide, we'll show you how to use Programmable SMSto send SMS and MMS messages in your Java web application. The code snippets in this guide are written using the Java SDK 7 or higher, and make use of the Twilio Java SDK.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eLet's get started!\u003c/p\u003e\u003c/div\u003e \u003c/div\u003e \u003cdiv\u003e\u003cdiv\u003e\u003c/div\u003e \u003c/div\u003e \u003cdiv\u003e\u003cdiv\u003e\u003ch2\u003eSign up for a Twilio Account\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003eTo use the Twilio REST API, you need an account. Signing up for a free Twilio account is easy. Once you've signed up, head over to your Console and grab your Account SID and your Auth Token. You will need those for the code samples below.\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003ePurchase an SMS Capable Phone Number\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003eSending SMS messages requires an SMS capable phone number. You can browse the available phone numbers in the Console. Be sure that the phone number you buy is SMS capable. When you search, you can check the box to filter available numbers to those that are SMS capable:\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cbr /\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eWhen viewing the search results, you can see the capability icons in the list of available numbers:\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cbr /\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eArmed with a Twilio phone number, you can now start sending messages to mobile devices.\u003c/p\u003e\u003c/div\u003e \u003c/div\u003e \u003cdiv\u003e\u003cdiv\u003e\u003ch2\u003eSend an SMS Message via the REST API\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003eSending an outgoing SMS message requires sending an HTTP POST to the Messages resource URI.                     <li>Send SMS and MMS Messages in Java </li> 
                    <ul></ul> 
                    <li>Related Guides </li>

                     <li>Track Delivery Status of Messages in Java </li> 
                     <li>Send Bulk SMS Messages in Java </li> 
                     <li>Receive and Reply to SMS and MMS Messages in Java </li>

               <div>
                <div>
                 <h1>Send SMS and MMS Messages in Java </h1> 
                 <div> 
                  <div>
                   <div>
                    <a id="change-detail-3" class="activity-detail__comment-link}"></a>
                    <ins>Agustin Camino </ins>
                   </div>
                   <a id="change-detail-4" class="activity-detail__comment-link}"></a>
                   <ins> </ins>
                  </div> 
                  <div></div> 
                 </div> 
                 <div>
                  <div>
                   <p>In this guide, we'll show you how to use&nbsp;Programmable SMSto&nbsp;send SMS and MMS messages in your Java web application. The code snippets in this guide are written using the Java SDK 7 or higher, and make use of the&nbsp;Twilio Java SDK.</p>
                   <p></p>
                   <p>Let's get started!</p>
                  </div> 
                 </div> 
                 <div>
                  <div></div> 
                 </div> 
                 <div>
                  <div>
                   <h2>Sign up for a Twilio Account</h2>
                   <p>To use the Twilio REST API, you need an account. Signing up for a free Twilio account is easy. Once you've signed up, head over to your Console and grab your Account SID and your Auth Token. You will need those for the code samples below.</p>
                   <h2>Purchase an SMS Capable Phone Number</h2>
                   <p>Sending SMS messages requires an SMS capable phone number. You can browse the available phone numbers in the Console. Be sure that the phone number you buy is SMS capable. When you search, you can check the box to filter available numbers to those that are SMS capable:</p>
                   <p><br></p>
                   <p>When viewing the search results, you can see the capability icons in the list of available numbers:</p>
                   <p><br></p>
                   <p>Armed with a Twilio phone number, you can now start sending messages to mobile devices.</p>
                  </div> 
                 </div> 
                 <div>
                  <div>
                   <h2>Send an SMS Message via the REST API</h2>
                   <p>Sending an outgoing SMS message requires sending an HTTP POST to the Messages&nbsp;resource URI. Using the helper library,&nbsp;you can create a new instance of the <b>Message</b> resource and specify the <b>To</b>, <b>From</b>, and <b>Body</b> parameters for your message.</p>
                  </div> 
                 </div> 
                 <div>
                  <div>
                   <div>
                    <div>
                     <div>
                      Send an SMS using the Programmable SMS API 
                      <ul>
                       <li>Java</li> 
                      </ul> 
                     </div> 
                     <div>
                      SDK Version: 
                      <ul>
                       <li>6.x</li> 
                       <li>7.x</li> 
                      </ul> 
                     </div> 
                     <pre><code>//  <a id="change-detail-5" class="activity-detail__comment-link}"></a><ins>You may want to be more specific in your importsimport java.util.*; import com.twilio.sdk.*; import com.twilio.sdk.resource.factory.*; import com.twilio.sdk.resource.instance.*; import com.twilio.sdk.resource.list.*; import java.util.ArrayList; import java.util.List; import org.apache.http.NameValuePair; import org.apache.http.message.BasicNameValuePair</ins>   <a id="change-detail-6" class="activity-detail__comment-link}"></a><del>Install the Java helper library from twilio.com/docs/java/installimport com.twilio.Twilio; import com.twilio.rest.api.v2010.account.Message; import com.twilio.type.PhoneNumber</del> ; public class <a id="change-detail-7" class="activity-detail__comment-link}"></a><ins>TwilioTest</ins> <a id="change-detail-8" class="activity-detail__comment-link}"></a><del>Example</del> { // Find your Account Sid and Token at twilio.com/user/account public static final String ACCOUNT_SID = "ACXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX"; public static final String AUTH_TOKEN = "your_auth_token"; public static void main(String[]args)  <a id="change-detail-9" class="activity-detail__comment-link}"></a><ins>throws TwilioRestException { TwilioRestClient client = new TwilioRestClient</ins>  <a id="change-detail-10" class="activity-detail__comment-link}"></a><del>{ Twilio.init</del> (ACCOUNT_SID, AUTH_TOKEN);                    <div>
                    <h5><i></i> Send an SMS using the Programmable SMS API </h5> 
                    <div></div> 
                   </div> 
                  </div> 
                 </div> 
                 <div>
                  <div>
                   <p>If you want to send a message to several recipients, you could simply create an array of&nbsp;recipients and iterate through each phone number in that array. You can send as many messages as you like, as fast as you like and Twilio will queue them up for delivery at your prescribed rate limit. See our guide on how to Send Bulk SMS Messagesfor more tips.</p>
                  </div> 
                 </div> 
                 <div>
                  <div>
                   <h2>Send a Message with Media (MMS)</h2>
                   <p>It's also easy to send an outgoing MMS using Twilio. To send an MMS, you also&nbsp;make an HTTP POST request to the Messages resourcebut this time specify a parameter for the URL of media, such as an image.</p>
                   <p><i>MMS messages can only be sent and received by numbers having MMS capability.</i> You can check the capabilities of numbers in the account portal or query the Available Phone Numbers resource to search for Twilio numbers that are MMS enabled.</p>
                  </div> 
                 </div> 
                 <div>
                  <div>
                   <div>
                    <div>
                     <div>
                      Send a Message with an Image URL 
                      <ul>
                       <li>Java</li> 
                      </ul> 
                     </div>

                      SDK Version: 
                      <ul>
                       <li>6.x</li> 
                       <li>7.x</li> 
                      </ul>

                    <h5><i></i> Send SMS during voice call </h5> 
                    <div></div> 
                   </div> 
                  </div> 
                 </div> 
                 <div>
                  <div>
                   <p>If you were to visit that webhook url in your browser, you would see TwiML that looks like this:</p>
                  </div> 
                 </div> 
                 <div>
                  <div>
                   <div>
                    <pre>&lt;?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?&gt; &lt;Response&gt; &lt;Say&gt;Hello! You will get an SMS message soon.&lt;/Say&gt; &lt;Sms&gt;This is the ship that made the Kessel Run in fourteen parsecs?&lt;/Sms&gt; &lt;/Response&gt; </pre>
                   </div> 
                  </div> 
                 </div> 
                 <div>
                  <div>
                   <p>Save a publicly-accessible URL to return that XML. Then, configure that URL to be the Voice URL of your Twilio phone number.</p>
                   <p>Call that number from a mobile phone -- you should hear a message <i>and</i> get a text message in response.</p>
